<div class="side-box-text plainlist"><b>This article contains <a class="mw-selflink selflink">Indic text</a>.</b> Without proper <a href="/wiki/Help:Multilingual_support_(Indic)" title="Help:Multilingual support (Indic)">rendering support</a>, you may see <a href="/wiki/Mojibake" title="Mojibake">question marks or boxes</a>, misplaced vowels or missing conjuncts instead of Indic text.</div></div>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Phrase_sanskrit.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="779" data-file-width="680" decoding="async" height="252" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Phrase_sanskrit.svg/220px-Phrase_sanskrit.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Phrase_sanskrit.svg/330px-Phrase_sanskrit.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Phrase_sanskrit.svg/440px-Phrase_sanskrit.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Phrase_sanskrit.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Sanskrit Phrase in different Brahmic Scripts.</div></div></div>
<p>The <b>Brahmic scripts</b>, also known as <b>Indic scripts</b>, are a family of <a href="/wiki/Abugida" title="Abugida">abugida</a> <a href="/wiki/Writing_system" title="Writing system">writing systems</a>. They are used throughout the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> and parts of <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asia</a>. They are descended from the <a href="/wiki/Brahmi_script" title="Brahmi script">Brahmi script</a> of ancient <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> and are used by various languages in several language families in <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>: <a href="/wiki/Indo-Aryan_languages" title="Indo-Aryan languages">Indo-Aryan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dravidian_languages" title="Dravidian languages">Dravidian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tibeto-Burman_languages" title="Tibeto-Burman languages">Tibeto-Burman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mongolic_languages" title="Mongolic languages">Mongolic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austroasiatic_languages" title="Austroasiatic languages">Austroasiatic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_languages" title="Austronesian languages">Austronesian</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tai_languages" title="Tai languages">Tai</a>. They were also the source of the <a href="/wiki/Collation" title="Collation">dictionary order</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Goj%C5%ABon" title="Gojūon">gojūon</a></i>) of <a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">Japanese</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Kana" title="Kana">kana</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Frellesvig_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-Frellesvig-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p>
<div aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading" class="toc" id="toc" role="navigation"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brahmic_scripts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Brahmic scripts descended from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Br%C4%81hm%C4%AB_script" title="Brāhmī script">Brahmi script</a>. Brahmi is clearly attested from the 3rd century BCE during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Ashoka" title="Ashoka">Ashoka</a>, who used the script <a href="/wiki/Edicts_of_Ashoka" title="Edicts of Ashoka">for imperial edicts</a>, but there are some claims of <a href="/wiki/Early_Indian_epigraphy" title="Early Indian epigraphy">earlier epigraphy</a> found on pottery in southern India and <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>. The most reliable of these were short Brahmi inscriptions dated to the 4th century BCE and published by <a href="/wiki/Robin_Coningham" title="Robin Coningham">Coningham</a> et al. (1996).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Coningham_1996_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Coningham_1996-2">[2]</a></sup> 
Northern Brahmi gave rise to the <a href="/wiki/Gupta_script" title="Gupta script">Gupta script</a> during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gupta_period" title="Gupta period">Gupta period</a>, which in turn diversified into a number of cursives during the <a href="/wiki/Middle_kingdoms_of_India" title="Middle kingdoms of India">medieval period</a>. Notable examples of such medieval scripts, developed by the 7th or 8th century, include <a href="/wiki/N%C4%81gar%C4%AB_script" title="Nāgarī script">Nagari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siddha%E1%B9%83_script" title="Siddhaṃ script">Siddham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sharada_script" title="Sharada script">Sharada</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Siddha%E1%B9%83_script" title="Siddhaṃ script">Siddhaṃ script</a> was especially important in <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, as many <a href="/wiki/Sutra" title="Sutra">sutras</a> were written in it. The art of Siddham <a href="/wiki/Calligraphy" title="Calligraphy">calligraphy</a> survives today in <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>. The tabular presentation and <a href="/wiki/Collation" title="Collation">dictionary order</a> of the modern <i><a href="/wiki/Kana" title="Kana">kana</a></i> system of Japanese writing is believed to be descended from the Indic scripts, most likely through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spread_of_Buddhism" title="Spread of Buddhism">spread of Buddhism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Frellesvig_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-Frellesvig-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p><p>Southern Brahmi evolved into the <a href="/wiki/Kadamba_script" title="Kadamba script">Kadamba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pallava_script" title="Pallava script">Pallava</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vatteluttu" title="Vatteluttu">Vatteluttu</a> scripts, which in turn diversified into other scripts of South India and Southeast Asia. Brahmic scripts spread in a peaceful manner, <a href="/wiki/Indianization_of_Southeast_Asia" title="Indianization of Southeast Asia">Indianization</a>, or the spread of Indian learning. The scripts spread naturally to Southeast Asia, at ports on trading routes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Court_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Court-3">[3]</a></sup> At these trading posts, ancient inscriptions have been found in Sanskrit, using scripts that originated in India. At first, inscriptions were made in Indian languages, but later the scripts were used to write the local Southeast Asian languages. Hereafter, local varieties of the scripts were developed. By the 8th century, the scripts had diverged and separated into regional scripts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spread_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Spread-4">[4]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 235px"><div style="width: 235px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 230px;"><div style="margin:50.5px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Asokan_brahmi_pillar_edict.jpg" title="A fragment of Ashoka's 6th pillar edict, in Brahmi, the ancestor of all Brahmic scripts"><img alt="A fragment of Ashoka's 6th pillar edict, in Brahmi, the ancestor of all Brahmic scripts" data-file-height="715" data-file-width="1598" decoding="async" height="89" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Asokan_brahmi_pillar_edict.jpg/200px-Asokan_brahmi_pillar_edict.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Asokan_brahmi_pillar_edict.jpg/300px-Asokan_brahmi_pillar_edict.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Asokan_brahmi_pillar_edict.jpg/400px-Asokan_brahmi_pillar_edict.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Characteristics">Characteristics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brahmic_scripts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Characteristics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1045330069" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="sidebar nomobile nowraplinks" style="width:auto;"><tbody><tr><th class="sidebar-title"><a href="/wiki/Calligraphy" title="Calligraphy">Calligraphy</a></th></tr><tr><td class="sidebar-content plainlist" style="padding-left:1.5em;padding-right:1.5em;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Arabic_calligraphy" title="Arabic calligraphy">Arabic</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chinese_calligraphy" title="Chinese calligraphy">Chinese</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Georgian_calligraphy" title="Georgian calligraphy">Georgian</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Indian_calligraphy" title="Indian calligraphy">Indian</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Islamic_calligraphy" title="Islamic calligraphy">Islamic</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Japanese_calligraphy" title="Japanese calligraphy">Japanese</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Korean_calligraphy" title="Korean calligraphy">Korean</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mongolian_calligraphy" title="Mongolian calligraphy">Mongolian</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Persian_calligraphy" title="Persian calligraphy">Persian</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tibetan_calligraphy" title="Tibetan calligraphy">Tibetan</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_calligraphy" title="Vietnamese calligraphy">Vietnamese</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Western_calligraphy" title="Western calligraphy">Western</a></li></ul></td>
</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1063604349" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Calligraphy" title="Template:Calligraphy"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Calligraphy" title="Template talk:Calligraphy"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Calligraphy&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Some characteristics, which are present in most but not all the scripts, are:
</p>
<ul><li>Each <a href="/wiki/Consonant" title="Consonant">consonant</a> has an inherent vowel which is usually a short ‘<a href="/wiki/Schwa" title="Schwa">ə</a>’ (in <a href="/wiki/Bengali_language" title="Bengali language">Bengali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assamese_language" title="Assamese language">Assamese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Odia_language" title="Odia language">Odia</a>, the phoneme is /<a href="/wiki/Open-mid_back_rounded_vowel" title="Open-mid back rounded vowel">ɔ</a>/ due to sound shifts). Other vowels are written by adding to the character. A <a href="/wiki/Diacritic" title="Diacritic">mark</a>, known in <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Virama" title="Virama">virama</a>/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Halanta" title="Halanta">halanta</a>, can be used to indicate the absence of an inherent vowel.</li>
<li>Each vowel has two forms, an independent form when not attached to a consonant, and a dependent form, when attached to a consonant. Depending on the script, the dependent forms can be either placed to the left of, to the right of, above, below, or on both the left and the right sides of the base consonant.</li>
<li>Consonants (up to 4 in Devanagari) can be combined in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ligature_(typography)" title="Ligature (typography)">ligatures</a>. Special marks are added to denote the combination of 'r' with another consonant.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nasalization" title="Nasalization">Nasalization</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aspiration_(phonetics)" title="Aspiration (phonetics)">aspiration</a> of a consonant's dependent vowel is also noted by separate signs.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Alphabetical_order" title="Alphabetical order">alphabetical order</a> is: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vowels" title="Vowels">vowels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Velar_consonant" title="Velar consonant">velar consonants</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palatal_consonants" title="Palatal consonants">palatal consonants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Retroflex_consonant" title="Retroflex consonant">retroflex consonants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dental_consonant" title="Dental consonant">dental consonants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bilabial_consonant" title="Bilabial consonant">bilabial consonants</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Approximants" title="Approximants">approximants</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sibilants" title="Sibilants">sibilants</a>, and other consonants. Each consonant grouping had four <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stop_consonant" title="Stop consonant">stops</a> (with all four possible values of voicing and aspiration), and a <a href="/wiki/Nasal_consonant" title="Nasal consonant">nasal consonant</a>.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Comparison">Comparison</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brahmic_scripts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Comparison">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Below are comparison charts of several of the major Indic scripts, organised on the principle that glyphs in the same column all derive from the same Brahmi glyph.  Accordingly:
</p>
<ul><li>The charts are not comprehensive. Glyphs may be unrepresented if they do not derive from any Brahmi character, but are later inventions.</li>
<li>The pronunciations of glyphs in the same column may not be identical.  The pronunciation row is only representative; the <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">International Phonetic Alphabet</a> (IPA) pronunciation is given for <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> where possible, or another language if necessary.</li></ul>
<p>The transliteration is indicated in <a href="/wiki/ISO_15919" title="ISO 15919">ISO 15919</a>.
</p>

<dl><dt>Notes</dt></dl>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-iso-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-iso_5-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This list tries to include characters of same origins, not same sounds. In <a href="/wiki/Bengali_alphabet" title="Bengali alphabet">Bengali</a> র is pronounced as <i>rô</i> but it is originally <i>va</i> which is still used for <i>wa</i> sound in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mithilakshar" title="Mithilakshar">Mithilakshar</a> and modern <a href="/wiki/Assamese_alphabet" title="Assamese alphabet">Assamese</a> ৱ (wabbô) was derived from middle Assamese র (wô). Compare with জ (ja) য (ya) and য় (ẏ) which are pronounced as <i>jô</i>,  <i>jô</i> and <i>yô</i> in Bengali and <i>zô</i>, <i>zô</i> and <i>yô</i> in Assamese respectively. য is related to Devanagari य (ya) and it is still pronounced as "ya" in Mithilakshar. Since their sounds shifted, the dots were added to keep the original sounds.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Meitei-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Meitei_6-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">includes supplementary consonants not in contemporary use</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Chakma-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Chakma_7-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">inherent vowel is ā</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-thai-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-thai_8-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-thai_8-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-thai_8-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-thai_8-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-thai_8-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-thai_8-5"><sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-thai_8-6"><sup><i><b>g</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-thai_8-7"><sup><i><b>h</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-thai_8-8"><sup><i><b>i</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Modified forms of these letters are or were used for distinctions made in Thai; these distinctions are not made for Sanskrit and Pali in the Thai script.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-lao-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-lao_9-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-lao_9-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-lao_9-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-lao_9-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-lao_9-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-lao_9-5"><sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-lao_9-6"><sup><i><b>g</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-lao_9-7"><sup><i><b>h</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-lao_9-8"><sup><i><b>i</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-lao_9-9"><sup><i><b>j</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-lao_9-10"><sup><i><b>k</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-lao_9-11"><sup><i><b>l</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-lao_9-12"><sup><i><b>m</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-lao_9-13"><sup><i><b>n</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">These letters are obsolete, but were used mainly for Sanskrit and Pali in the Lao script.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-jav-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-jav_10-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-jav_10-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-jav_10-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-jav_10-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-jav_10-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-jav_10-5"><sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-jav_10-6"><sup><i><b>g</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-jav_10-7"><sup><i><b>h</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-jav_10-8"><sup><i><b>i</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-jav_10-9"><sup><i><b>j</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-jav_10-10"><sup><i><b>k</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-jav_10-11"><sup><i><b>l</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-jav_10-12"><sup><i><b>m</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-jav_10-13"><sup><i><b>n</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Letters used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Javanese" title="Old Javanese">Old Javanese</a>. They are now obsolete, but are used for honorifics in contemporary Javanese.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-su-kha-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-su-kha_11-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Invented new character to represent the Arabic letter <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%D8%AE" title="خ">خ</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-su-old-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-su-old_12-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Letter used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Sundanese" title="Old Sundanese">Old Sundanese</a>. It is now obsolete.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-su-sya-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-su-sya_13-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Invented new character. Actually to represent the Arabic letter <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%D8%B4" title="ش">ش</a>, which has similar pronunciation with śa.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vowels">Vowels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brahmic_scripts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Vowels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Vowels are presented in their independent form on the left of each column, and in their corresponding dependent form (vowel sign) combined with the consonant <i>k</i> on the right. A glyph for <i>ka</i> is an independent consonant letter itself without any vowel sign, where the vowel <i>a</i> is <a href="/wiki/Inherent_vowel" title="Inherent vowel">inherent</a>.
</p>
<table class="wikitable Unicode" style="text-align:center; font-size:100%;width:100%;overflow:auto">
<tbody><tr>
<th rowspan="2">ISO</th>
<th colspan="2"><a href="/wiki/A_(Indic)" title="A (Indic)">a</a></th>
<th colspan="2"><a href="/wiki/%C4%80_(Indic)" title="Ā (Indic)">ā</a></th>
<th colspan="2"><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%8A_(Indic)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ê (Indic) (page does not exist)">ê</a></th>
<th colspan="2"><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%94_(Indic)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ô (Indic) (page does not exist)">ô</a></th>

<p><b>Notes</b>
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1011085734" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-vrare-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-vrare_14-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-vrare_14-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-vrare_14-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Letters for <i>r̥̄</i>, <i>l̥</i>, <i>l̥̄</i> and a few others are obsolete or very rarely used.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Meitei-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Meitei_15-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">includes supplementary vowels not in contemporary use</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-vkhmer-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-vkhmer_16-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">When used to write their own languages, Khmer can have either an <i>a</i> or an <i>o</i> as the inherent vowel, following the rules of its orthography.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-vthailao-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-vthailao_17-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-vthailao_17-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Thai and Lao scripts do not have independent vowel forms, for syllables starting with a vowel sound, a "zero" consonant, อ and ອ, respectively, to represent the glottal stop /ʔ/.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-su-vowel-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-su-vowel_18-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-su-vowel_18-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-su-vowel_18-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-su-vowel_18-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Letters used in Old Sundanese. They are now obsolete. </span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_Brahmic_scripts">List of Brahmic scripts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brahmic_scripts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: List of Brahmic scripts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical">Historical</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brahmic_scripts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Historical">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Brahmi script was already divided into regional variants at the time of the earliest surviving epigraphy around the 3rd century BC. Cursives of the Brahmi script began to diversify further from around the 5th century AD and continued to give rise to new scripts throughout the Middle Ages. The main division in antiquity was between northern and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tamil_Brahmi" title="Tamil Brahmi">southern Brahmi</a>. In the northern group, the <a href="/wiki/Gupta_script" title="Gupta script">Gupta script</a> was very influential, and in the southern group the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vatteluttu_alphabet" title="Vatteluttu alphabet">Vatteluttu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kadamba_script" title="Kadamba script">Kadamba</a>/<a href="/wiki/Pallava_script" title="Pallava script">Pallava</a> scripts with the <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_Southeast_Asia" title="Hinduism in Southeast Asia">spread of Buddhism</a> sent Brahmic scripts throughout Southeast Asia.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Northern_Brahmic">Northern Brahmic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brahmic_scripts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Northern Brahmic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Indoarische_Sprachen_Gruppen.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="919" data-file-width="877" decoding="async" height="419" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Indoarische_Sprachen_Gruppen.png/400px-Indoarische_Sprachen_Gruppen.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Indoarische_Sprachen_Gruppen.png/600px-Indoarische_Sprachen_Gruppen.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Indoarische_Sprachen_Gruppen.png/800px-Indoarische_Sprachen_Gruppen.png 2x" width="400"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Indoarische_Sprachen_Gruppen.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map of Indo-Aryan languages using their respective Brahmic family scripts (except dark blue colored Khowar, Pashai, Kohistani, and Urdu, not marked here, which use Arabic-derived scripts).</div></div></div>
